## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: The task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. This is the core problem of chemical kinetics where rate laws describe how reaction rates depend on reactant concentrations, with possible time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed first-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with constant production/consumption)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (net rate from forward and reverse reactions)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing reaction orders)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Photochemical decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (power-law time dependence in rate constant)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)
- Combined time and concentration: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * t (additive time-dependent source term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate proportional to concentration power → nth-order irreversible decay: dA_dt = -k * A^n
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium: terms like k_f*A - k_r or k*(A - A_eq)
- Rate with concentration in both numerator and denominator → enzyme or surface-catalyzed reaction with saturation
- Product of concentration and (constant minus concentration) → autocatalytic or logistic growth kinetics
- Explicit time dependence multiplying concentration terms → non-isothermal reaction or time-varying external forcing
- Sum of terms with different powers of A → parallel competing reactions of different orders
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches zero with concave-down shape → fractional-order kinetics A^n with 0 < n < 1
- Oscillatory behavior in rate vs time → coupled reaction network or periodic forcing, consider trigonometric terms like sin(c0*t)
